gt; Class IA and IB cytochrome C signature
gp; PRINTS; PR00603 CYTOCHROMEC1; PR00605 CYTCHROMECIC; PR00606 CYTCHROMECID
gp; PRINTS; PR00607 CYTCHROMECIE; PR00608 CYTCHROMECII; PR00609 CYTOCHROMEC3
gp; PRINTS; PR00610 CYTOCHROMEF
gp; INTERPRO; IPR002327
gp; PROSITE; PS00190 CYTOCHROME_C
gp; PDB; 155C; 1C2R; 1CCR; 1YEA; 2C2C; 5CYT
gp; SCOP; 155C; 1C2R; 1CCR; 1YEA; 2C2C; 5CYT
gp; CATH; 155C; 1C2R; 1CCR; 1YEA; 2C2C; 5CYT
bb;
gr; 1. PETTIGREW, G.W. AND MOORE, G.R.
gr; Cytochromes c. Biological Aspects.
gr; SPRINGER-VERLAG, BERLIN-HEIDELBERG-NEW YORK (1987).
gr;
gr; 2. AMBLER, R.P.
gr; Sequence variability in bacterial cytochromes c.
gr; BIOCHIM.BIOPHYS.ACTA 1058 42-47 (1991).
gr;
gr; 3. MOORE, G.R. AND PETTIGREW, G.W.
gr; Cytochromes c. Evolutionary, Structural, and Physicochemical Aspects. 
gr; SPRINGER-VERLAG, BERLIN-HEIDELBERG-NEW YORK (1990).
bb;
bb;
gd; Cytochromes c (cyt c) can be defined as electron-transfer proteins having
gd; one or several haem c groups, bound to the protein by one or, more
gd; generally, two thioether bonds involving sulphydryl groups of cysteine
gd; residues. The fifth haem iron ligand is always provided by a histidine
gd; residue. Cyt c possess a wide range of properties and function in a large
gd; number of different redox processes [1].
gd;
gd; Ambler [2] recognised four classes of cyt c. Class I includes the low-spin
gd; soluble cyt c of mitochondria and bacteria, with the haem-attachment site
gd; towards the N-terminus, and the sixth ligand provided by a methionine
gd; residue about 40 residues further on towards the C-terminus. On the basis
gd; of sequence similarity, class I cyt c were further subdivided into five
gd; classes, IA to IE. Class IB includes the eukaryotic mitochondrial cyt c
gd; and prokaryotic "short" cyt c2 exemplified by Rhodopseudomonas globiformis
gd; cyt c2; Class IA includes "long" cyt c2, such as Rhodospirillum rubrum
gd; cyt c2 and Aquaspirillum itersonii cyt c-550, which have several extra
gd; loops by comparison with Class IB cyt c.
gd;
gd; The 3D structures of a considerable number of class IA and IB cyt c have
gd; been determined [3]. The proteins consist of 3-6 alpha-helices; the three
gd; most conserved "core" helices form a "basket" around the haem group, with
gd; one haem edge exposed to the solvent. Most class I cyt c have conserved
gd; aromatic residues clustered around the haem and axial ligands [3].
gd;
gd; CYTCHRMECIAB is a 6-element fingerprint that provides a signature for class
gd; IA and IB cyt c. The fingerprint was derived from an initial alignment of 33
gd; sequences: motif 1 is situated in the loop between helices 1 and 2, and
gd; includes two invariant Cys residues, which covalently bind the haem group,
gd; and the His residue that provides the fifth haem iron ligand (cf. PROSITE
gd; pattern CYTOCHROME_C); motifs 3-6 contain conserved aromatic residues, the
gd; Trp residue of motif 4 being invariant among the mitochondrial cyt c; and
gd; motif 5 includes an invariant Met, which provides the sixth haem iron ligand.
gd; Three iterations on OWL28.0 were required to reach convergence, at which
gd; point a true set comprising 132 sequences was identified. Several partial
gd; matches were also found: CYC_KLULA, CYC_NEUCR, C550_NITWI and A56280 lack
gd; motif 6; CY2_RHORU, NRL_2C2C, CY2_RHOSH and C551_ERYSP lack motif 3;
gd; CYC_TRYBB lacks motif 1; RSU35437 is an R.sphaeroides cyt c fragment that
gd; matches the first three motifs; and the sequences matching only 2 motifs
gd; are class I cyt c that neither belong to class IA or IB.
gd;
gd; An update on SPTR37_9f identified a true set of 107 sequences, and 42
gd; partial matches.
bb;

bb;
bb;
gd; Flavoprotein pyridine nucleotide cytochrome reductases [1] (FPNCR) catalyse
gd; the interchange of reducing equivalents between one-electron carriers and
gd; the two-electron-carrying nicotinamide dinucleotides. The enzymes include
gd; ferredoxin:NADP+ reductases (FNR); plant and fungal NAD(P)H:nitrate
gd; reductases; NADH:cytochrome b5 reductases; NADPH:P450 reductases;
gd; NADPH:sulfite reductases; nitric oxide synthases; phthalate dioxygenase 
gd; reductase; and various other flavoproteins.
gd;
gd; Dioxygen can be incorporated directly into organic compounds in reactions
gd; catalysed by enzymes termed oxygenases or hydroxylases: oxygenases that
gd; catalyse the incorporation of both atoms of dioxygen into substrates are
gd; known as dioxygenases; those that catalyse the incorporation of only one
gd; atom of dioxygen are termed monooxygenases, or mixed-function oxygenases.
gd; The second atom of dioxygen is reduced to H2O either by the substrates
gd; themselves or by a co-substrate reductant [2].
gd;
gd; Electron transfer components of a number of bacterial multi-component 
gd; aromatic-ring and alkyl-group oxygenases (including phenol hydroxylase [3],
gd; benzoate 1,2-dioxygenase [4], toluate 1,2-dioxygenase [5], xylene 
gd; monooxygenase [6] and methane monooxygenase [7]), belong to family of 
gd; [2Fe-2S] ferredoxin/FPNCR fusion proteins. Other members of the family are 
gd; Yersinia pseudotuberculosis CDP-6-deoxy-3,4-glucoseen reductase [8] and 
gd; S.typhimurium rfbI protein [9]. All contain a [2Fe-2S] ferredoxin domain
gd; fused to the N-terminus of an FPNCR domain. The direction of electron flow
gd; is from flavin to the [2Fe-2S] center. 
gd;
gd; PHEHYDRXLASE is a 6-element fingerprint that provides a signature for the
gd; phenol hydroxylase family. The fingerprint was derived from an initial
gd; alignment of 7 sequences: the motifs were drawn solely from the FPNCR
gd; domain - motifs 1-3 span the flavin-binding domain, and motifs 4-6 encode
gd; the NAD(H)-binding domain. Motifs 1, 2, 4, 5 and 6 correspond to FPNCR
gd; motifs 1, 2, 4, 5 and 8, respectively. Motif 2 appears to be involved in
gd; binding the isoalloxazine ring of FAD; motif 4 includes residues involved
gd; in binding the diphosphate group of the pyridine nucleotide; and motif 6
gd; contains a conserved Cys residue that may interact with NAD(H) and is
gd; necessary for efficient electron transfer [10]. Two iterations on OWL26.2
gd; were required to reach convergence, at which point a true set comprising 11
gd; sequences was identified. Several partial matches were also found:
gd; reductase components of Pseudomonas putida naphthalene dioxygenase (JN0640,
gd; JN0642) and polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbon dioxygenase (A55217) lack motif
gd; 2; and Pseudomonas pickettii toluene-3-monooxygenase reductase (PPU04052)
gd; and Vibrio alginolyticus Na+-translocating NADH-quinone reductase 
gd; (VIBNQR363) lack motif 5. Surprisingly, the mmoC component of Methylosinus 
gd; trichosporium methane monooxygenase (C48360), which is functionally 
gd; identical to the mmoC protein of Methylococcus capsulatus (MEMC_METCA), 
gd; lacks motifs 5 and 6 (motif 6 is well conserved among most FPNCRs).
gd; Pseudomonas cepacia 2-halobenzoate 1,2-dioxygenase reductase (PCCBDABC3)
gd; lacks motifs 2 and 5; Pseudomonas mendocina toluene-4-monooxygenase
gd; component tmoF (A47016) and Pseudomonas pseudoalcaligenes phenoxybenzoate
gd; dioxygenase pobB (S44172) lack motifs 3 and 5. All these proteins are
gd; [2Fe-2S] ferredoxin/FPNCR fusion enzymes, except S44172, which has a
gd; [2Fe-2S] ferredoxin domain at its C-terminus. 
gd;
gd; An update on SPTR37_9f identified a true set of 19 sequences, and 146
gd; partial matches.

gr; 1. SHORT, M.N., TURNER, D.S., MARCH, J.F., PAPPIN, D.J.C., PARENTE, A.
gr; AND DAVIES, J.W.
gr; The primary structure of papaya mosaic viurs coat protein.
gr; VIROLOGY 152(1) 280-283 (1986).
gr; 
gr; 2. SKRYABIN, K.G., KRAEV, A.S., MOROZOV, S.YU., ROZANOV, M.N.,
gr; CHERNOV, B.K., LUKASHEVA, L.I. AND ATABEKOV, J.G.
gr; The nucleotide sequence of potato viurs X RNA.
gr; NUCLEIC ACIDS RES. 16 10929-10930 (1988).
gr;
gr; 3. MEMELINK, J., VAN DER VLUGT, C.I., LINTHORST, H.J., DERKS, A.F.,
gr; ASJES, C.J. AND BOL, J.F.
gr; Homologies between the genomes of a carlavirus (lily symptomless virus)
gr; and a potexvirus (lily virus X) from lily plants.
gr; J.GEN.VIROL. 71(4) 917-924 (1990).
bb;
bb;
gd; Potex viruses are encapsidated, single-stranded RNA plant viruses. The
gd; group includes papaya mosaic virus [1], potato virus X [2] and lily virus
gd; X [3]. Sequence comparison of potexvirus coat proteins with those of
gd; carlaviruses (e.g., lily symptomless virus [3]) show considerable
gd; similarity. The most highly conserved region of potex and carlavirus coat
gd; proteins lies around the middle third of the sequences: this is a
gd; relatively aromatic- and proline-rich region and contains a single
gd; conserved cysteine residue.
gd;
gd; POTXCARLCOAT is a 4-element fingerprint that provides a signature for the
gd; potex virus coat protein. The fingerprint was derived from an initial
gd; alignment of 6 sequences: the motifs were drawn from conserved regions
gd; within the middle third of the alignment, motifs 3 and 4 spanning the
gd; region encoded by PROSITE pattern POTEX_CARLAVIRUS_COAT (PS00418). Three
gd; iterations on OWL23.2 were required to reach convergence, at which point a
gd; true set comprising 38 sequences was identified. Several partial matches
gd; were also found, all of which are family members.
gd;
gd; An update on SPTR37_9f identified a true set of 84 sequences, and 10
gd; partial matches.
bb;

gx; PR00834

ga; 19-MAR-1998; UPDATE 23-JUN-1999
gt; HtrA/DegQ protease family signature
gp; INTERPRO; IPR001940
bb;
gr; 1. LIPINSKA, B., SHARMA, S. AND GEORGOPOULOS, C. 
gr; Sequence analysis and regulation of the htrA gene of Escherichia coli:
gr; a sigma 32-independent mechanism of heat-inducible transcription. 
gr; NUCLEIC ACIDS RES. 16 10053-10067 (1988). 
gr;
gr; 2. LIPINSKA, B., ZYLICZ, M. AND GEORGOPOULOS, C.
gr; The htrA (DegP) protein, essential for Escherichia coli survival at high
gr; temperatures, is an endopeptidase.
gr; J.BACTERIOL. 172 1791-1797 (1990). 
gr; 
gr; 3. WALLER P.R. AND SAUER R.T.
gr; Characterization of DegQ and DegS, Escherichia coli genes encoding 
gr; homologs of the DegP protease. 
gr; J.BACTERIOL. 178 1146-1153 (1996). 
bb;
bb;
gd; The E.coli htrA gene product (or DegP protein) is essential for bacterial
gd; survival at temperatures above 42 degrees [1,2]. The htrA gene has been 
gd; sequenced and an open reading frame coding for a protein of 491 amino acids
gd; identified [1]. The protein has an N-terminal sequence typical of a leader
gd; peptide. The HtrA protein has been shown to be a specific endopeptidase 
gd; that is inhibited by diisopropylfluorophosphate, suggesting that HtrA is
gd; a serine protease [2]. 
gd;
gd; The degQ and degS genes of E.coli encode proteins of 455 and 355 residues
gd; that are homologues of the DegP protease [3]. Purified DegQ protein has the
gd; properties of a serine endoprotease, and is processed by the removal of a
gd; 27-residue N-terminal signal sequence. Deletion studies suggest that DegQ,
gd; like DegP, functions as a periplasmic protease in vivo [3].
gd;
gd; PROTEASES2C is a 6-element fingerprint that provides a signature for the
gd; htrA/degQ family of serine proteases. The fingerprint was derived from
gd; an initial alignment of 12 sequences: the motifs were drawn from conserved
gd; regions spanning the central portion of the alignment - motif 1 includes
gd; the catalytic histidine; motif 2 contains the catalytic Asp; and motif 4
gd; includes the catalytic Ser. Three iterations on OWL30.0 were required to
gd; reach convergence, at which point a true set comprising 40 sequences was
gd; identified. Several partial matches were also found, all of which appear
gd; to be related proteases that fail to match one or more motifs.
gd;
gd; An update on SPTR37_9f identified a true set of 41 sequences, and 25
gd; partial matches.
bb;
bb;

gt; Kir1.1 inward rectifier K+ channel signature
gp; PRINTS; PR00169 KCHANNEL; PR01333 2POREKCHANEL
gp; PRINTS; PR01320 KIRCHANNEL; PR01322 KIR12CHANNEL; PR01323 KIR13CHANNEL
gp; PRINTS; PR01324 KIR21CHANNEL; PR01325 KIR22CHANNEL; PR01326 KIR23CHANNEL
gp; PRINTS; PR01327 KIR31CHANNEL; PR01328 KIR32CHANNEL; PR01329 KIR33CHANNEL
gp; PRINTS; PR01330 KIR34CHANNEL; PR01678 KIR5CHANNEL; PR01331 KIR61CHANNEL
gp; PRINTS; PR01332 KIR62CHANNEL; PR01679 KIR7CHANNEL
bb;
gr; 1. MINOR, D.L., JR., MASSELLING, S.J., JAN, Y.N. AND JAN, L.Y.
gr; Transmembrane structure of an inwardly rectifying potassium channel.
gr; CELL 96 879-891 (1999).
gr; 
gr; 2. DOUPNIK, C.A., DAVIDSON, N. AND LESTER, H.A.
gr; The inward rectifier potassium channel family.
gr; CURR.OPIN.NEUROBIOL. 5 268-277 (1995).
gr;
gr; 3. REIMANN, F. AND ASHCROFT, F.M.
gr; Inwardly rectifying potassium channels.
gr; CURR.OPIN.CELL BIOL. 11 503-508 (1999).
bb;
bb;
gd; Potassium channels are found in virtually all cell types. Their pore-
gd; forming subunits fall into three structural families, i.e. those possessing
gd; six, four and two transmembrane (TM) domains. The six-TM domain K+ channels
gd; can be further subdivided into six families: the voltage-gated K+ channels
gd; (Kv), the KCNQ channels, the eag-like K+ channels, and three Ca2+-activated
gd; K+ channels. Inwardly-rectifying K+ channels (Kir) are the principal class
gd; of two-TM domain K+ channels, and the recently-discovered two-pore domain
gd; K+ channels, make up a family of four-TM domain K+ channels.
gd;
gd; Inwardly rectifying potassium channels (Kir) are responsible for regulating
gd; diverse processes including: cellular excitability, vascular tone, heart
gd; rate, renal salt flow, and insulin release [1]. To date, around twenty
gd; members of this superfamily have been cloned, which can be grouped into six
gd; families by sequence similarity - these are designated Kir1.x-7.x [2,3].
gd; 
gd; Cloned Kir channel cDNAs encode proteins of between ~370-500 residues,
gd; containing two predicted TM domains, with the characteristic K+ channel
gd; pore-forming domain located between them. Both N- and C-termini are thought
gd; to be cytoplasmic, and the N-terminus lacks a signal sequence. It is thought
gd; that four Kir subunits assemble to form a tetrameric channel complex, which
gd; may be hetero- or homomeric [1].
gd;
gd; Kir1.1 channels (also known as ROMK1-6 and KAB-1) are thought to underlie
gd; K+ secretion in the kidney. Their activity is modulated by intracellular
gd; pH, with acidosis inhibiting the channel. Both N- and C-termini are thought
gd; to be involved in this modulation. Mutations in Kir1.1 lead to Bartter's
gd; syndrome type III, an inherited kidney disorder, which leads to salt-
gd; wasting, hypokalaemia and metabolic acidosis. All of the mutations that
gd; have been functionally characterised either abolish, or markedly reduce,
gd; Kir1.1 K+ currents.
gd;
gd; KIR11CHANNEL is a 7-element fingerprint thar provides a signature for the
gd; Kir1.1 inward rectifier K+ channel. The fingerprint was derived from an
gd; initial alignment of 2 sequences: the motifs were drawn from conserved
gd; regions spanning virtually the full alignment length, focusing on those 
gd; sections that characterise Kir1.1 but distinguish it from other subtypes - 
gd; motif 1 lies in the putative cytoplasmic N-terminus; motif 2 spans the
gd; C-terminal portion of the extracellular loop, and the start of the second
gd; TM domain; and motifs 3-7 encode portions of the cytoplasmic C-terminus.
gd; Two iterations on SPTR37_10f were required to reach convergence, at which
gd; point a true set comprising 3 sequences was identified.
bb;

gx; PR01370
gn; COMPOUND(9)
ga; 13-JUL-2000
gt; Translocated intimin receptor (Tir) signature
gp; 
bb;
gr; 1. HUECK, C.J.
gr; Type III protein secretion systems in bacterial pathogens of animals and 
gr; plants.
gr; MICROBIOL.MOL.BIOL.REV. 379-433 (1998).
gr; 
gr; 2. BATCHELOR, M., PRASANNAN, S., DANIELL, S., REECE, S., CONNERTON, I.,
gr; BLOOMBERG, G., DOUGAN, G., FRANKEL, G. AND MATTHEWS, S.
gr; Structural basis for recognition of the translocated intimin receptor (Tir) 
gr; by the intimin from enteropathogenic Escherichia coli.
gr; EMBO J. 19 2452-2464 (2000).
bb;
bb;
gd; Secretion of virulence factors in Gram-negative bacteria involves 
gd; transportation of the protein across two membranes to reach the cell 
gd; exterior [1]. There have been four secretion systems described in 
gd; animal enteropathogens, such as Salmonella and Yersinia, with further 
gd; sequence similarities in plant pathogens like Ralstonia and Erwinia [1].
gd;
gd; The type III secretion system is of great interest, as it is used to 
gd; transport virulence factors from the pathogen directly into the host cell 
gd; [1] and is only triggered when the bacterium comes into close contact with
gd; the host. The protein subunits of the system are very similar to those of 
gd; bacterial flagellar biosynthesis [1]. However, while the latter forms a
gd; ring structure to allow secretion of flagellin and is an integral part of
gd; the flagellum itself [1], type III subunits in the outer membrane 
gd; translocate secreted proteins through a channel-like structure.
gd;
gd; Exotoxins secreted by the type III system do not possess a secretion signal,
gd; and are considered unique for this reason [1]. Enteropathogenic and entero-
gd; haemorrhagic Escherichia coli secrete the translocated intimin receptor
gd; (Tir) [1]. The bacterial adhesion molecule, intimin, targets Tir, which is
gd; embedded in the target cell's plasma membrane [2], and allows the 
gd; bacterial cell to attach to the host.
gd;
gd; TRNSINTIMINR is a 9-element fingerprint that provides a signature for the 
gd; translocated intimin receptors. The fingerprint was derived from an initial
gd; alignment of 2 sequences: the motifs were drawn from conserved regions 
gd; spanning the full alignment length (~550 amino acids). Two iterations on
gd; SPTR37_10f were required to reach convergence, at which point a true set
gd; comprising 6 sequences was identified.
bb;

gp; MIM; 610594

gr; 1. BABA, M., HONG, S.-B., SHARMA, N., WARREN, M.B., NICKERSON, M.L., 
gr; IWAMATSU, A., ESPOSITO, D., GILLETTE, W.K., HOPKINS, R.F. III., HARTLEY, 
gr; J.L., FURIHATA, M., OISHI, S., ZHEN, W., BURKE, T.R. JR., LINEHAN, W.M., 
gr; SCHMIDT, L.S. AND ZBAR, B.
gr; Folliculin encoded by the BHD gene interacts with a binding protein, FNIP1, 
gr; and AMPK, and is involved in AMPK and mTOR signaling.
gr; PEROC NALTL ACAD. SCI. U.S.A. 103 15552-15557 (2006)
gr;
gr; 2. HASUMI, H., BABA, M., HONG, S.-B., HASUMI, Y., HUANG, Y., YAO, M., 
gr; VALERA, V.A., LINEHAN, W.M. AND SCHMIDT, L.S.
gr; Identification and characterization of a novel folliculin-interacting 
gr; protein FNIP2.
gr; GENE 415 60-67 (2008).
bb;
bb;
gd; Birt-Hogg-Dube' syndrome, a disorder characterised by benign tumours 
gd; of the hair follicle, lung cysts and renal neoplasia, is caused by germline
gd; mutations in the BHD(FLCN) gene; this encodes a tumour suppressor
gd; protein, folliculin (FLCN), of unknown function [1]. The folliculin-
gd; interacting protein, FNIP1, has also been identified and shown to interact
gd; with 5' AMP-activated protein kinase (AMPK), which plays a vital role in
gd; energy sensing [1]. Together, then, it is thought that folliculin (mutated
gd; in Birt-Hogg-Dube' syndrome) and its interaction partner, FNIP1, may be
gd; involved in energy and/or nutrient sensing via the AMPK and mTOR
gd; signalling pathways.
gd;
gd; FNIP1 has a homologue, FNIP2, which also interacts with FLCN and 
gd; AMPK. C-terminally-deleted FLCN mutants, like those produced by 
gd; germline mutations in BHD patients, do not bind FNIP2, suggesting
gd; that FLCN tumour-suppressor function may be facilitated by interactions
gd; with both FNIP1 and FNIP2 via its C-terminus [2]. FNIP1 and FNIP2 are 
gd; able to form homo- or heteromeric multimers, and may hence function
gd; either independently or cooperatively with FLCN [2]. 
gd;
gd; FOLLICULNIP1 is a 5-element fingerprint that provides a signature for 
gd; folliculin-interacting protein 1. The fingerprint was derived from an
gd; initial alignment of 9 sequences: the motifs were drawn from conserved
gd; regions spanning the central and C-terminal portions of the alignment -
gd; motifs 1 and 2 lie centrally, and motifs 3-5 lie in the C-terminal region.
gd; Two iterations on SPTR57_40f were required to reach convergence, at which
gd; point a true set comprising 12 sequences was identified. Two partial matches
gd; were also found, B3KX44_HUMAN and Q5RDH0_PONAB, human and orang-utan
gd; homologues that fail to match 2 or more motifs.
